# Renamed DMCP tables, fixed data quality bugs, froze canonical IDs, built `dmcp-listings.qmd`, updated `build_facility_crosswalk()`, completed DMCP canonical matching (170 matched, 60 new IDs 1001–1060), then loaded the DDP daily population feather file (661,928 rows, 853 facility codes, 2023-09-01 to 2025-10-15). Confirmed `detention_facility_code` is structurally identical to DETLOC. Classified all 853 codes: 160 direct DETLOC matches via `dmcp_canonical_map`, 66 high-confidence name matches against FY19-26 canonical list, 186 hospital/medical facilities, 171 ERO hold rooms, 23 BOP federal prisons, and 238 unmatched detention facilities.

## User

other pages start with data at y = 1.\\n\\n.parse_dmcp_pdf_page <- function(page_tokens, data_y_min) {\\n  assign_col <- function(x_val) {\\n    idx <- findInterval(x_val, .dmcp_pdf_col_breaks, rightmost.closed = FALSE)\\n    .dmcp_pdf_col_names[idx]\\n  }\\n\\n  toks <- page_tokens |>\\n    dplyr::filter(y >= data_y_min) |>\\n    dplyr::arrange(y, x) |>\\n    dplyr::mutate(col = assign_col(x))\\n\\n  if (nrow(toks) == 0) return(tibble::tibble())\\n\\n  # New record when y-gap > 1 pt. Each facility spans a main row and a\\n  # DETLOC sub-row offset by 1 pt; inter-record gap is ≥ 2 pt.\\n  toks <- toks |>\\n    dplyr::mutate(record_id = cumsum(c(TRUE, diff(y) > 1)))\\n\\n  toks |>\\n    dplyr::group_by(record_id, col) |>\\n    dplyr::summarise(value = paste(text, collapse = \\\" \\\"), .groups = \\\"drop\\\") |>\\n    tidyr::pivot_wider(names_from = col, values_from = value, Good coverage of the data. Here's the picture:

**Overlap**

180 of the facilities appear in both lists — 86% of faclist15 and 90% of faclist17. 29 are only in faclist15, 21 only in faclist17.

**Location consistency for shared facilities**

Mostly clean. No state mismatches at all. The issues:

- **12 ZIP mismatches** — all in northeastern states (NJ, MA, ME, NH, VT). These are the leading-zero stripping artifact: faclist15 ZIPs were stored as integers, dropping the leading zero (e.g., `07601` → `7601`). Not a real discrepancy. This is a known quirk of the 2015 XLSX source.
- **2 city mismatches** — both minor: `"Colorado Spring"` (truncated) vs. `"Colorado Springs"`, and `"Kearney"` vs. `"Kearny"` (NJ). The latter is a real data entry variant.
- **5 name mismatches** — all legitimate renamings between 2015 and 2017, e.g. Adelanto changed from "Adelanto Detention Facility" to "Adelanto ICE Processing Center", and Otay Mesa got a simplified name.

**Facilities unique to each list**

The faclist15-only facilities (29) are almost entirely USMS IGA (18) and IGSA (11) — local county jails under USMS intergovernmental agreements. They're scattered across CA, AZ, CO, LA, PA, and a handful of other states. The pattern suggests these were de-authorized USMS jail agreements that weren't renewed by 2017.

The faclist17-only facilities (21) are more interesting: they include **4 DIGSAs** (Folkston GA, Pine Prairie LA, Cibola NM, Prairieland TX) — dedicated, purpose-built private detention centers that were newly contracted between 2015 and 2017. Texas also picked up 5 new facilities (LaSalle, Prairieland, Taylor, Titus, Tom Green, Webb). The USMS IGA closures and DIGSA additions suggest a shift away from opportunistic local jail use toward dedicated contracted capacity.

This helper handles both.\n  parse_adp <- function(x) {\n    if (is.numeric(x)) return(round(x, 1))\n    as.numeric(stringr::str_remove_all(as.character(x), \",\"))\n  }\n\n  adp_cols <- dplyr::intersect(\n    names(df),\n    c(\"fy17_adp\", \"fy16_adp\", \"fy15_adp\", \"fy14_adp\",\n      \"fy13_adp\", \"fy12_adp\", \"fy11_adp\", \"fy10_adp\",\n      \"facility_population_count\")\n  )\n\n  df |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      dplyr::across(dplyr::all_of(adp_cols), parse_adp),\n      facility_capacity_as_needed = grepl("},"elapsedMs":599}</script></tool-result></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01YH4B534J6wXzmnspMch2MZ"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 13.7KB, 313 lines, showing lines 1-313]\n     1→# Build a canonical facility crosswa...[truncated, total 15371 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 13.7KB, 313 lines, showing lines 1-313]\n# Build a canonical facility crosswalk across all years.\n#\n# Matching strategy (two passes):\n#   1. Exact match on facility_name + facility_city + facility_state\n#   2. Within the same ZIP code, fuzzy address string similarity (OSA >= 0.80)\n#      resolves cases where the same physical facility appears under a different\n#      name in different years.\n#\n# Returns a list with two elements:\n#   $crosswalk  — maps every (name, city, state) variant to canonical_id/name\n#   $presence   — one row per canonical facility; TRUE/FALSE for each fiscal year\n\nyear_order <- c(\"FY19\", \"FY20\", \"FY21\", \"FY22\", \"FY23\", \"FY24\", \"FY25\", \"FY26\")\n\n# ── Do-not-merge pairs ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# Genuinely distinct facilities that share a ZIP and similar addresses.\n\ndo_not_merge_pairs <- function() {\n  tibble::tribble(\n    ~name_a,                              ~name_b,\n    \"Folkston Main IPC\",                  \"Annex - Folkston IPC\",\n    \"Folkston Main IPC\",                  \"Folkston Annex IPC\",\n    \"Main - Folkston IPC (D Ray James)\",  \"Annex - Folkston IPC\",\n    \"Main - Folkston IPC (D Ray James)\",  \"Folkston Annex IPC\",\n    \"Joe Corley Processing Center\",       \"Montgomery ICE Processing Center\",\n    \"Joe Corley ICE Processing Center\",   \"Montgomery ICE Processing Center\"\n  )\n}\n\n# ── Canonical name overrides ─────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\ncanonical_name_overrides_table <- function() {\n  tibble::tribble(\n    ~lookup_name,                                          ~canonical_name,                                        ~canonical_city,  ~canonical_state,\n    \"Adams County Detention Center\", County Sheriff Department.\",                    \"Baker County Sheriff's Office\",                         \"Macclenny\",      \"FL\",\n    \"Buffalo (Batavia) Service Processing Center\",         \"Buffalo (Batavia) Service Processing Center\",           \"Batavia\",        \"NY\",\n    \"Farmville Detention Center\",                          \"Farmville Detention Center\",                            \"Farmville\",      \"VA\",\n    \"Northwest ICE Processing Center\",                     \"Northwest ICE Processing Center\",                       \"Tacoma\",         \"WA\"\n  )\n}\n\n# ── Union-Find helpers ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nnew_union_find <- function(ids) {\n  parent <- stats::setNames(ids, ids)\n  env <- new.env(parent = emptyenv())\n  env$parent <- parent\n  env\n}\n\nuf_find <- function(uf, x) {\n  while (uf$parent[as.character(x)] != x) x <- uf$parent[as.character(x)]\n  x\n}\n\nuf_union <- function(uf, a, b) {\n  ra <- uf_find(uf, a)\n  rb <- uf_find(uf, b)\n  if (ra != rb) uf$parent[as.character(ra)] <- rb\n}\n\n# ── Main crosswalk builder ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nbuild_facility_crosswalk <- function(facilities_data_list) {\n  # Pool all distinct (name, city, state, address, zip) combos\n  all_facilities_norm <- facilities_data_list |>\n    purrr::imap_dfr(\\(df, yr) df |>\n      dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state,\n                    facility_address, facility_zip) |>\n      dplyr::mutate(year = yr)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      zip5      = stringr::str_pad(facility_zip, width = 5, side = \"left\", pad = \"0\"),\n      addr_norm = stringr::str_to_upper(stringr::str_trim(stringr::str_squish(facility_address)))\n    )\n\n  # Pass 1: provisional ID per exact name+city+state combo\n  facility_key_exact <- all_facilities_norm |>\n    dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state, addr_norm, zip5) |>\n    dplyr::distinct() |>\n    dplyr::group_by(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state) |>\n    dplyr::summarise(addr_norm = dplyr::first(addr_norm),\n                     zip5 = dplyr::first(zip5),\n                     .groups = \"drop\") |>\n    dplyr::mutate(facility_id = dplyr::row_number())\n\n  # Pass 2: fuzzy address merge within same ZIP\n  merge_candidates <- facility_key_exact |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(addr_norm), !is.na(zip5)) |>\n    dplyr::group_by(zip5) |>\n    dplyr::filter(dplyr::n() > 1) |>\n    dplyr::group_modify(\\(grp, key) {\n      n <- nrow(grp)\n      pairs <- expand.grid(i = seq_len(n), j = seq_len(n)) |> dplyr::filter(i < j)\n      pairs |> dplyr::transmute(\n        facility_id_a = grp$facility_id[i],\n        facility_id_b = grp$facility_id[j],\n        addr_a        = grp$addr_norm[i],\n        addr_b        = grp$addr_norm[j],\n        addr_dist     = stringdist::stringdist(addr_a, addr_b, method = \"osa\"),\n        addr_sim      = 1 - addr_dist / pmax(nchar(addr_a), nchar(addr_b))\n      )\n    }) |>\n    dplyr::ungroup()\n\n  strong_addr_matches <- merge_candidates |> dplyr::filter(addr_sim >= 0.80)\n\n  # Apply do-not-merge exclusions\n  dnm <- do_not_merge_pairs() |>\n    dplyr::left_join(facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_id),\n                     by = c(\"name_a\" = \"facility_name\")) |>\n    dplyr::rename(id_a = facility_id) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_id),\n                     by = c(\"name_b\" = \"facility_name\")) |>\n    dplyr::rename(id_b = facility_id)\n\n  strong_addr_matches <- strong_addr_matches |>\n    dplyr::anti_join(dnm, by = c(\"facility_id_a\" = \"id_a\", \"facility_id_b\" = \"id_b\")) |>\n    dplyr::anti_join(dnm, by = c(\"facility_id_a\" = \"id_b\", \"facility_id_b\" = \"id_a\"))\n\n  # Union-Find to cluster facility_ids\n  uf <- new_union_find(facility_key_exact$facility_id)\n  for (i in seq_len(nrow(strong_addr_matches))) {\n    uf_union(uf, strong_addr_matches$facility_id_a[i],\n             strong_addr_matches$facility_id_b[i])\n  }\n\n  canonical_map <- tibble::tibble(facility_id = facility_key_exact$facility_id) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(canonical_id = purrr::map_int(facility_id, \\(x) uf_find(uf, x)))\n\n  # Choose canonical name: most-recent year's name per cluster\n  all_facilities_keyed <- all_facilities_norm |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state, facility_id),\n      by = c(\"facility_name\", \"facility_city\", \"facility_state\")\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_map, by = \"facility_id\")\n\n  canonical_names <- all_facilities_keyed |>\n    dplyr::mutate(year_rank = match(year, year_order)) |>\n    dplyr::group_by(canonical_id) |>\n    dplyr::slice_max(year_rank, n = 1, with_ties = FALSE) |>\n    dplyr::ungroup() |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id,\n                  canonical_name = facility_name,\n                  canonical_city = facility_city,\n                  canonical_state = facility_state)\n\n  # Apply manual overrides\n  overrides <- canonical_name_overrides_table() |>\n    dplyr::left_join(facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_id),\n                     by = c(\"lookup_name\" = \"facility_name\")) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_map, by = \"facility_id\") |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state) |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(canonical_id))\n\n  canonical_names <- canonical_names |>\n    dplyr::rows_update(overrides, by = \"canonical_id\", unmatched = \"ignore\")\n\n  # Final crosswalk\n  facility_crosswalk <- facility_key_exact |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_map, by = \"facility_id\") |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_names, by = \"canonical_id\") |>\n    dplyr::select(facility_id, canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state,\n                  facility_name, facility_city, facility_state)\n\n  message(glue::glue(\n    \"Canonical facilities: {dplyr::n_distinct(facility_crosswalk$canonical_id)}\",\n    \" (from {nrow(facility_key_exact)} exact name+city+state variants,\",\n    \" {nrow(strong_addr_matches)} address-based merges)\"\n  ))\n\n  facility_crosswalk\n}\n\n# ── Attach canonical IDs to each year's data ────────────────────────────────\n\nattach_canonical_ids <- function(facilities_data_list, facility_crosswalk) {\n  purrr::imap(facilities_data_list, \\(df, yr) {\n    df |>\n      dplyr::left_join(\n        facility_crosswalk |>\n          dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state,\n                        canonical_id, canonical_name),\n        by = c(\"facility_name\", \"facility_city\", \"facility_state\")\n      )\n  })\n}\n\n# ── Facility presence and trajectory ─────────────────────────────────────────\n\nbuild_facility_presence <- function(facilities_keyed) {\n  year_cols_present <- year_order[year_order %in% names(facilities_keyed)]\n  if (length(year_cols_present) == 0) {\n    year_cols_present <- year_order\n  }\n  first_year       <- head(year_cols_present, 1)\n  most_recent_year <- tail(year_cols_present, 1)\n\n  presence <- facilities_keyed |>\n    purrr::imap_dfr(\\(df, yr) df |>\n      dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name) |>\n      dplyr::distinct() |>\n      dplyr::mutate(year = yr)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(present = TRUE) |>\n    tidyr::pivot_wider(names_from = year, values_from = present,\n                       values_fill = FALSE, names_sort = FALSE) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name, dplyr::any_of(year_cols_present)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(n_years = rowSums(dplyr::across(dplyr::any_of(year_cols_present))))\n\n  # first_seen / last_seen\n  presence <- presence |>\n    dplyr::rowwise() |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      first_seen = year_cols_present[dplyr::c_across(dplyr::any_of(year_cols_present))][1],\n      last_seen  = tail(year_cols_present[dplyr::c_across(dplyr::any_of(year_cols_present))], 1)\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::ungroup()\n\n  # trajectory\n  presence <- presence |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      trajectory = dplyr::case_when(\n        first_seen == first_year & last_seen == most_recent_year &\n          n_years == length(year_cols_present) ~ \"continuous\",\n        first_seen == first_year & last_seen == most_recent_year ~ \"persistent_gaps\",\n        first_seen == first_year & last_seen != most_recent_year ~ \"closed\",\n        first_seen != first_year & last_seen == most_recent_year ~ \"new\",\n        TRUE ~ \"transient\"\n      )\n    )\n\n  # n_years_current: consecutive years ending at most_recent_year\n  presence <- presence |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      n_years_current = apply(\n        dplyr::pick(dplyr::all_of(year_order[year_order %in% names(presence)])),\n        1, function(row) {\n          if (!isTRUE(row[most_recent_year])) return(0L)\n          count <- 0L\n          for (yr in rev(year_order[year_order %in% names(presence)])) {\n            if (isTRUE(row[yr])) count <- count + 1L else break\n          }\n          count\n        })\n    )\n\n  # n_years_initial: consecutive years from first_year\n  presence <- presence |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      n_years_initial = apply(\n        dplyr::pick(dplyr::all_of(year_order[year_order %in% names(presence)])),\n        1, function(row) {\n          if (!isTRUE(row[first_year])) return(0L)\n          count <- 0L\n          for (yr in year_order[year_order %in% names(presence)]) {\n            if (isTRUE(row[yr])) count <- count + 1L else break\n          }\n          count\n        })\n    )\n\n  presence\n}\n\n# ── Build panel dataset ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nbuild_panel <- function(facilities_keyed) {\n  facilities_keyed |>\n    purrr::imap_dfr(\\(df, yr) df |> dplyr::mutate(fiscal_year = yr)) |>\n    dplyr::relocate(fiscal_year, canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                    facility_name, facility_city, facility_state)\n}\n\n# ── Canonical facility list ──────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# One row per canonical facility: the most recent year's address columns,\n# plus canonical_id and canonical_name from the crosswalk.\n# This is the authoritative input for geocoding — kept separate from the\n# full panel so downstream steps never have to reduce it themselves.\n\nbuild_canonical_facilities <- function(facilities_panel) {\n  facilities_panel |>\n    dplyr::mutate(year_rank = match(fiscal_year, year_order)) |>\n    dplyr::group_by(canonical_id) |>\n    dplyr::slice_max(year_rank, n = 1, with_ties = FALSE) |>\n    dplyr::ungroup() |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip)\n}\n\n# ── Save outputs to data/ ───────────────────────────────────────────────────\n\nsave_outputs <- function(facility_crosswalk, facility_presence, facilities_panel) {\n  paths <- c(\n    \"data/facility_crosswalk.rds\",\n    \"data/facility_crosswalk.csv\",\n    \"data/facility_presence.rds\",\n    \"data/facility_presence.csv\",\n    \"data/facilities_panel.rds\",\n    \"data/facilities_panel.csv\"\n  )\n  saveRDS(facility_crosswalk, paths[1])\n  write.csv(facility_crosswalk, paths[2], row.names = FALSE)\n  saveRDS(facility_presence, paths[3])\n  write.csv(facility_presence, paths[4], row.names = FALSE)\n  saveRDS(facilities_panel, paths[5])\n  write.csv(facilities_panel, paths[6], row.names = FALSE)\n  message(\"Saved: \", paste(basename(paths), collapse = \", \"))\n  paths\n}\n"},"elapsedMs":77}</script></tool-result></div>

facility_zip = stringr::str_pad(

)

So both should work.

A comparison table of shared columns vs. each-list-only columns.\n\n### Section 3 — Overlap analysis\n- Venn summary: 180 shared, 29 faclist15-only, 21 faclist17-only\n- Verification that location fields agree for shared facilities (city, state, ZIP, and the 5 legitimate name changes)\n- Formatted tables of faclist15-only and faclist17-only facilities ← **this is where the user visually confirms that none of the \"only\" facilities are actually duplicates of each other under different DETLOC codes** (see note below)\n\n### Section 4 — Connection to canonical facility list *(placeholder)*\nTo be filled in after the matching work below.\n\n---\n\n## Step-by-step plan for canonical list integration\n\n### Step 1: Visual confirmation that \"only\" facilities don't overlap\n\nThe DETLOC analysis already proves the two \"only\" sets share no DETLOC codes, but two facilities with *different* DETLOC codes could still be the same physical facility (DETLOC reassignments are rare but not impossible). Present the 29 faclist15-only and 21 faclist17-only facilities in a side-by-side or combined formatted table in the QMD, sorted by state. The user reviews visually and confirms no hidden duplicates before we proceed.\n\nWe can also run a quick fuzzy name+state match between the two \"only\" sets programmatically (flag any pairs with OSA similarity ≥ 0.70 on name within the same state) to narrow down what needs visual attention.\n\n### Step 2: Match faclist15 and faclist17 to the existing canonical list\n\nThe existing `facility_crosswalk` is built entirely from FY19–FY26 annual stats and contains ~250 canonical facilities. DMCP facilities span FY2010–FY2017, so there will be both matches (facilities that were active in both eras) and genuinely new entries. Matching approach, in order:\n\n1. **Exact name+city+state** match to `canonical_facilities` → strongest possible match\n2. **Fuzzy address within ZIP** (OSA ≥ 0.80) → catches renamed facilities at the same address\n3. **Fuzzy name within state** (fallback) → last resort; flag for manual review rather than auto-assign\n\nReport: how many match, how many are new to the canonical list. Flag all fuzzy matches for inspection before committing.\n\n### Step 3: Assign canonical IDs to new facilities\n\nFacilities in faclist15/17 that don't match any existing canonical entry get new IDs. Design decision (needs your input, see open question #1 below):\n\n**Proposed approach:** Continue the integer sequence from `max(existing_canonical_id) + 1`. Do not regenerate the existing IDs. The new IDs are assigned in a separate function and stored in a new lookup table — they are never derived from `row_number()` on the combined set, which would make them unstable.\n\nCreate `data/canonical_id_registry.csv`: a persistent, append-only file mapping `canonical_id` → `canonical_name`, `canonical_city`, `canonical_state`. This is the authoritative source for canonical IDs going forward, replacing the implicit numbering in `build_facility_crosswalk()`.\n\n### Step 4: Add `detloc` to the canonical list\n\nOnce canonical IDs are assigned to all DMCP facilities, we can add a `detloc` column to the master list. Check:\n- How many of the ~250 FY19–FY26 canonical facilities can be matched to a DETLOC? (Expect most active-since-2015 facilities to match, but post-2017 openings and facilities that were never in DMCP won't have one.)\n- If a canonical facility matches rows in both faclist15 and faclist17, confirm the DETLOC codes agree (they should, but this is worth verifying).\n\nThe uniqueness constraint is: one `canonical_id` → at most one `detloc`, and one `detloc` → exactly one `canonical_id`.\n\n### Step 5: Add `canonical_id` to faclist15 and faclist17\n\nAfter matching:\n- `faclist15` and `faclist17` both get a `canonical_id` column (NA for any unmatched rows, if any remain after manual review)\n- These become new pipeline targets: `faclist15_keyed`, `faclist17_keyed`\n\n### Step 6: Build the master facility list\n\nA new pipeline target (`master_facility_list`) with one row per canonical facility across *all* sources:\n\n| Column | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| `canonical_id` | Unique integer |\n| `canonical_name` | Most recent name |\n| `canonical_city`, `canonical_state` | Most recent location |\n| `detloc` | DMCP code (NA if no DMCP record) |\n| `in_faclist15`, `in_faclist17` | Logical flags |\n| `in_fy_panel` | Logical: present in any of FY19–FY26 |\n| `first_fy_adp`, `last_fy_adp` | First and last fiscal year with ADP data across all sources |\n\nSave as `data/master_facility_list.rds/.csv`. Add to `save_outputs()`.\n\n---\n\n## Pipeline changes\n\nNew targets to add to `_targets.R` (in a new \"── Canonical integration ──\" section):\n\n```r\ntar_target(faclist15_keyed, attach_dmcp_canonical_ids(faclist15, dmcp_canonical_map)),\ntar_target(faclist17_keyed, attach_dmcp_canonical_ids(faclist17, dmcp_canonical_map)),\ntar_target(dmcp_canonical_map, build_dmcp_canonical_map(faclist15, faclist17, facility_crosswalk)),\ntar_target(master_facility_list, build_master_facility_list(facility_crosswalk, dmcp_canonical_map))\n```\n\nNew functions (in a new file, `R/integrate.R`):\n- `build_dmcp_canonical_map()` — performs the matching in Steps 2–4\n- `attach_dmcp_canonical_ids()` — joins map onto a faclist tibble\n- `build_master_facility_list()` — assembles the unified list\n\n---\n\n## Open questions / things I think are missing or would make this stronger\n\n### 1. Before we extend the canonical list and start propagating IDs outward (to faclist15/17, to Wikipedia targets, etc.), we should decide: do we freeze the existing IDs (write them to a persistent registry) or accept that they might shift? Freezing now, before the integration work, would be much cheaper than fixing downstream references later.\n\n### 2. The QMD is a natural place to display these — a formatted table of \"proposed matches\" with similarity scores that you can inspect and approve or veto. Some facilities that appear in faclist17 may have closed before FY19 and won't be in the panel at all. Others may have opened after July 2017 and won't be in faclist17. These two groups are worth flagging explicitly in the master list.\n\n### 4. Looking at the PDF parser, the ZIPs come out as character strings from Tabula. But they're coming out as 3 or 4 characters and being left-padded to 5. The issue is that the PDF parser isn't reading the full ZIP code - it's reading truncated values.

Wait - "92301" from faclist15 for Adelanto CA is correct. But faclist17 shows "00923" for the same facility. 

So it looks like Tabula is only capturing the first 3 digits of each ZIP code before hitting a column boundary, then the padding logic is adding zeros to the left to make it 5 digits. That explains why "92301" becomes "00923" and "12211" becomes "00122" - the parser is truncating at the column break.

The PDF parser is only capturing the first 3 digits of the ZIP code for faclist17. This is a column boundary issue in the Tabula extraction. The ZIP column boundary (`.dmcp_pdf_col_breaks`) cuts off the ZIP column too early, so only the first 3 digits are captured.

```r
.dmcp_pdf_col_breaks <- c(
   34, 101, 151, 179, 206, 218, 228, 242, 260, 282,
  302,   # capacity
  320,   # population_count

```
"detloc", "name", "address", "city", "county", "state", "zip",
```

So the ZIP column comes before "type". Looking at the col_breaks:
- 0-34: detloc
- 34-101: name
- 101-151: address
- 151-179: city
- 179-206: county
- 206-218: state
- 218-228: zip
- 228-242: type
- ...

So ZIP is in the range 218-228 (10 points wide). A 5-digit ZIP at position 218 would need more space to fully capture all digits before the next column boundary at 228.

The ZIP column is allocated only 10 points of width, which isn't enough for a standard 5-digit ZIP code at typical font sizes. I need to expand the ZIP boundaries and shift the subsequent columns to accommodate the full width needed. The current code still has ZIP constrained to 218-228 points, which is too narrow for 5-digit codes. Extracting tables with tabulapdf...

The column breaks parameter in tabulapdf specifies the left edge x-position of each column boundary, so a ZIP range of 218-228 means the column only spans 10 points wide—clearly insufficient for capturing full ZIP codes. I need to widen this boundary to give the ZIP column adequate space.

Now I have everything I need. Let me write the QMD:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01CkoByHvPkY7oG2Si3ft1RH"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"write","input":{"file_path":"/Users/bjorkjcr/Dropbox (Personal)/R/ice-detention/dmcp-listings.qmd","content":"---\ntitle: \"ICE DMCP Facility Listings: Data Documentation and Integration\"\ndate: last-mod...[truncated, total 9329 chars]"},"caption":"dmcp-listings.qmd","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"---\ntitle: \"ICE DMCP Facility Listings: Data Documentation and Integration\"\ndate: last-modified\nformat:\n  html:\n    toc: true\n    toc-depth: 3\n    code-fold: true\nexecute:\n  echo: true\n  warning: false\n  message: false\n---\n\n```{r setup}\nlibrary(targets)\nlibrary(dplyr)\nlibrary(tidyr)\nlibrary(stringr)\nlibrary(knitr)\n\ntar_load(c(faclist15, faclist17))\n```\n\n## Overview\n\nThis document records the addition of two supplemental data sources to the ICE detention pipeline: point-in-time DMCP (Detention Management Compliance Program) facility authorization rosters from December 2015 and July 2017.\n\nThese are a different document type from the annual FY stats spreadsheets (FY2019–FY2026) that form the main panel. Rather than single-year snapshots, each is an authorization roster showing all currently authorized ICE detention facilities at a point in time, with historical ADP data spanning multiple fiscal years per row, alongside contract, operator, and inspection metadata.\n\nThe two lists are tracked as pipeline targets `faclist15` and `faclist17` (see `_targets.R`). Full provenance metadata is in `data/dmcp-listings.yml`.\n\n---\n\n## Data sources\n\n### faclist15 — December 2015 XLSX\n\n- **Title:** 2015 ICE Detention Facility Listing\n- **Source:** ICE FOIA reading room (`ice.gov/foia`)\n- **URL:** `https://www.ice.gov/doclib/foia/dfs/2015IceDetentionFacilityListing.xlsx`\n- **File:** `data/2015IceDetentionFacilityListing.xlsx`\n- **Data as of:** December 8, 2015\n- **Currency note:** FY2016 data reflects IIDS as of 12/08/2015 (approximately the first 70 days of FY2016); FY2015 and earlier reflect end-of-fiscal-year figures.\n- **Fiscal years covered:** FY2010–FY2016 (ADP columns `fy10_adp`–`fy16_adp`)\n\n### faclist17 — July 2017 PDF\n\n- **Title:** ICE DMCP Facility List — ERO Custody Management Division, FY2017\n- **Source:** Prison Legal News document library\n- **URL:** `https://www.prisonlegalnews.org/media/publications/ICE_DMCP_Facility_List_ERO_Custody_Management_Division_2017.pdf`\n- **File:** `data/ICE_DMCP_Facility_List_2017.pdf`\n- **Data as of:** July 10, 2017\n- **Currency note:** ADP figures reflect IIDS as of 07/10/2017; EID data through 07/08/2017.\n- **Fiscal years covered:** FY2010–FY2017 (ADP columns `fy10_adp`–`fy17_adp`)\n- **Parsing:** Extracted with `tabulapdf::extract_tables()` using explicit column boundaries derived from bounding-box coordinates of the PDF header row.\n\n---\n\n## Dataset summaries\n\n```{r summaries}\nbind_rows(\n  faclist15 |> summarise(\n    source = \"faclist15\",\n    rows = n(),\n    cols = ncol(faclist15),\n    fy_range = \"FY2010–FY2016\",\n    adp_cols = 7L\n  ),\n  faclist17 |> summarise(\n    source = \"faclist17\",\n    rows = n(),\n    cols = ncol(faclist17),\n    fy_range = \"FY2010–FY2017\",\n    adp_cols = 8L\n  )\n) |> kable(col.names = c(\"Source\", \"Rows\", \"Columns\", \"ADP range\", \"ADP columns\"))\n```\n\n### Facility type breakdown\n\n```{r type-breakdown}\nbind_rows(\n  faclist15 |> count(facility_type_detailed, sort = TRUE) |> mutate(source = \"faclist15\"),\n  faclist17 |> count(facility_type_detailed, sort = TRUE) |> mutate(source = \"faclist17\")\n) |>\n  pivot_wider(names_from = source, values_from = n, values_fill = 0L) |>\n  arrange(desc(faclist15)) |>\n  kable(col.names = c(\"Type\", \"faclist15\", \"faclist17\"))\n```\n\n**Type key:** IGSA = Intergovernmental Service Agreement (local jail); USMS IGA = USMS intergovernmental agreement; DIGSA = Dedicated IGSA (private, ICE-dedicated); CDF = Contract Detention Facility (private); SPC = Service Processing Center (ICE-operated); USMS CDF = USMS contract detention facility.\n\n### Column schema\n\nfaclist17 has two additional columns not in faclist15: `fy17_adp` (inserted after `facility_population_count`) and `cy16_rating` (inserted before `cy15_rating`). All other columns are shared.\n\n---\n\n## Overlap analysis\n\n### Summary\n\n```{r overlap-counts}\nboth_codes   <- intersect(faclist15$detloc, faclist17$detloc)\nonly15_codes <- setdiff(faclist15$detloc,   faclist17$detloc)\nonly17_codes <- setdiff(faclist17$detloc,   faclist15$detloc)\n\ntibble::tibble(\n  Category = c(\"Shared (both lists)\", \"Only in faclist15\", \"Only in faclist17\"),\n  Count    = c(length(both_codes), length(only15_codes), length(only17_codes))\n) |> kable()\n```\n\nOf faclist15's 209 facilities, **`r scales::percent(length(both_codes)/nrow(faclist15), accuracy=1)`** (180) also appear in faclist17. Of faclist17's 201 facilities, **`r scales::percent(length(both_codes)/nrow(faclist17), accuracy=1)`** (180) also appear in faclist15.\n\n### Location consistency for shared facilities\n\nAfter applying all data cleaning, shared facilities should have identical city, state, and ZIP values across the two lists. The table below shows any discrepancies.\n\n```{r location-check}\nlocation_check <- inner_join(\n  select(faclist15, detloc,\n         city15 = facility_city, state15 = facility_state, zip15 = facility_zip),\n  select(faclist17, detloc,\n         city17 = facility_city, state17 = facility_state, zip17 = facility_zip),\n  by = \"detloc\"\n) |>\n  mutate(\n    city_diff  = city15  != city17,\n    state_diff = state15 != state17,\n    zip_diff   = zip15   != zip17\n  )\n\ntibble::tibble(\n  Field  = c(\"City\", \"State\", \"ZIP\"),\n  Mismatches = c(sum(location_check$city_diff),\n                 sum(location_check$state_diff),\n                 sum(location_check$zip_diff))\n) |> kable()\n```\n\n### Facility renames between 2015 and 2017\n\nFive facilities appear in both lists under different names. All are plausible renames, not data errors.\n\n```{r name-changes}\ninner_join(\n  select(faclist15, detloc, state = facility_state, `Name (2015)` = facility_name),\n  select(faclist17, detloc, `Name (2017)` = facility_name),\n  by = \"detloc\"\n) |>\n  filter(`Name (2015)` != `Name (2017)`) |>\n  kable()\n```\n\n---\n\n## Facilities unique to each list\n\nThe 29 facilities only in faclist15 and 21 only in faclist17 represent facilities that were either de-authorized between December 2015 and July 2017, or newly authorized in that window. The tables below are formatted for visual inspection to confirm that none of the \"only\" facilities are the same physical location appearing under a different DETLOC code.\n\n### Only in faclist15 (absent from faclist17)\n\nThese 29 facilities were authorized in December 2015 but not in July 2017 — likely de-authorized or contract-lapsed in the intervening period. Nearly all are USMS IGA or IGSA facilities (local county jails under intergovernmental agreements), consistent with a contraction of the USMS jail-use model.\n\n```{r only15}\nfaclist15 |>\n  filter(detloc %in% only15_codes) |>\n  select(detloc, facility_name, facility_city, facility_state, facility_type_detailed) |>\n  arrange(facility_state, facility_name) |>\n  kable(col.names = c(\"DETLOC\", \"Name\", \"City\", \"State\", \"Type\"))\n```\n\n### Only in faclist17 (absent from faclist15)\n\nThese 21 facilities were authorized by July 2017 but not in December 2015. The four DIGSAs (dedicated ICE private facilities) in this group — Folkston IPC (GA), Pine Prairie (LA), Cibola (NM), and Prairieland (TX) — are particularly notable, representing new large-capacity contracted facilities added between 2015 and 2017. Texas accounts for five of the 21 new entries.\n\n```{r only17}\nfaclist17 |>\n  filter(detloc %in% only17_codes) |>\n  select(detloc, facility_name, facility_city, facility_state, facility_type_detailed) |>\n  arrange(facility_state, facility_name) |>\n  kable(col.names = c(\"DETLOC\", \"Name\", \"City\", \"State\", \"Type\"))\n```\n\n---\n\n## Section 4: Integration with canonical facility list {#sec-integration}\n\n> **Status: Planned — not yet implemented.**\n\nThe next phase of this work connects the two DMCP lists to the canonical facility identifiers used by the FY2019–FY2026 annual stats panel. Key steps:\n\n1. **Visual confirmation** that none of the 29 faclist15-only and 21 faclist17-only facilities are the same physical location under different DETLOC codes (tables above support this review).\n\n2. **Match to canonical list** — attempt exact name+city+state and fuzzy address matches between DMCP facilities and the `facility_crosswalk` (~348 canonical IDs, range 1–398, now frozen in `data/canonical_id_registry.csv`).\n\n3. **Assign new canonical IDs** — facilities in faclist15/17 with no match to the FY19–26 canonical list will receive new IDs starting at **1001**, keeping DMCP-sourced facilities in a distinct ID range. Future FY annual stats (FY27+) will continue the main sequence from 399.\n\n4. **Add `detloc` to canonical list** — once matched, add DETLOC codes to the canonical registry; show how many of the existing 348 FY19–26 facilities have a matching DETLOC.\n\n5. **Build master facility list** — one row per canonical facility across all sources, with columns for `canonical_id`, `canonical_name`, `detloc`, and logical flags for `in_faclist15`, `in_faclist17`, `in_fy_panel`.\n\n### Placeholder: DMCP fiscal-year ADP tables\n\nA future step (not yet planned in detail) will pivot the wide-format ADP columns in faclist15 and faclist17 into long-format per-facility-per-year rows, producing `faclist15_adp_long` and `faclist17_adp_long`. Because both lists share FY2010–FY2016, those years will appear in two sources and will require cross-checking for ADP consistency. FY2017 is faclist17-only. **Data quality fixes (4 bugs found and fixed):**
- `Kearney` → `Kearny` and `Colorado Spring` → `Colorado Springs` added to `fix_city_names()`
- The `Cottonwood Fall` regex was over-matching `"Falls"` → `"Fallss"` — fixed with `\b`
- `facility_state` can receive a leading character bleed from the county cell in the PDF — now stripped with `str_extract("[A-Z]{2}$")`
- The PDF column boundaries for zip/type/type_detailed/male_female were each 4–14 points too narrow, truncating ZIP codes to 3 digits — corrected from actual bounding-box coordinates

- `dmcp-listings.qmd` — living documentation document with source overview, dataset summaries, overlap analysis (with the side-by-side "only" tables for visual confirmation), and a placeholder Section 4 for the matching/integration work to come

Let me read the current `crosswalk.R` to understand what needs to change.

The key change is:
1. Load `canonical_id_registry.csv` at the start of `build_facility_crosswalk()`
2. When assigning `facility_id` (Pass 1, exact match on name+city+state), instead of using `row_number()`, look up the canonical_id from the registry for known facilities


3. For new facilities not in the registry, assign new IDs starting from `max(registry$canonical_id) + 1`

Now I'm thinking through the current workflow more carefully. The existing process pools distinct facility attributes across all years, then uses `row_number()` to assign provisional IDs in Pass 1 for exact name+city+state matches, followed by fuzzy address matching in Pass 2 that clusters facilities via union-find. The `canonical_map` then maps those provisional `facility_id` values to their final `canonical_id` (the root of each cluster), and `canonical_names` tracks the preferred name for each canonical ID.

The issue is that `canonical_id` values are just the unstable `facility_id` values from the cluster roots. Instead, I need to reference the `canonical_id_registry.csv` file to look up frozen IDs by canonical name, city, and state after building the crosswalk, and only generate new IDs for facilities that don't exist in the registry. I'm realizing the core issue: when canonical names shift between years, a simple name-based join won't reliably match registry entries. So I need a more flexible matching strategy that tries exact name matching first, then falls back to location-only matching for unmatched facilities, and finally assigns new IDs to anything still unmatched.

For the implementation, I'll need to modify the function signature to accept the registry as a parameter, probably reading it from the canonical ID registry file if not provided.

Then I'll update the targets pipeline to load that registry and pass it through. The core logic change is performing a left join against the registry to look up existing canonical IDs based on the facility's canonical name, city, and state combination, and assigning new IDs only for facilities that don't already exist in the registry.

The tricky part is that canonical names might shift between years, so matching by name alone could fail—I need a more stable lookup key, but the provisional IDs are exactly what I'm trying to replace, so I'll need to store something else in the registry to anchor the match.

The cleanest approach is to treat the registry as a permanent ID store paired with the canonical identity (name, city, state) at the time of assignment, then match new runs against that. The risk is if a facility's name changes between runs, the match fails and it gets a duplicate ID. I could handle this with historical variants or address proximity matching, but for now I'll assume canonical names are stable enough that this won't be a practical problem.

Given the scale here—348 facilities updated maybe once a year—the risk of name changes breaking ID stability is actually quite low. I'll go with matching by name+city+state first, assigning new IDs for non-matches, and emitting warnings so operators can manually fix the registry if a known facility accidentally gets a new ID due to a rename.

Pool all distinct (name, city, state, address, zip) combos\n  all_facilities_norm <- facilities_data_list |>\n    purrr::imap_dfr(\\(df, yr) df |>\n      dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state,\n                    facility_address, facility_zip) |>\n      dplyr::mutate(year = yr)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      zip5      = stringr::str_pad(facility_zip, width = 5, side = \"left\", pad = \"0\"),\n      addr_norm = stringr::str_to_upper(stringr::str_trim(stringr::str_squish(facility_address)))\n    )\n\n  # Pass 1: provisional ID per exact name+city+state combo\n  facility_key_exact <- all_facilities_norm |>\n    dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state, addr_norm, zip5) |>\n    dplyr::distinct() |>\n    dplyr::group_by(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state) |>\n    dplyr::summarise(addr_norm = dplyr::first(addr_norm),\n                     zip5 = dplyr::first(zip5),\n                     .groups = \"drop\") |>\n    dplyr::mutate(facility_id = dplyr::row_number())\n\n  # Pass 2: fuzzy address merge within same ZIP\n  merge_candidates <- facility_key_exact |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(addr_norm), !is.na(zip5)) |>\n    dplyr::group_by(zip5) |>\n    dplyr::filter(dplyr::n() > 1) |>\n    dplyr::group_modify(\\(grp, key) {\n      n <- nrow(grp)\n      pairs <- expand.grid(i = seq_len(n), j = seq_len(n)) |> dplyr::filter(i < j)\n      pairs |> dplyr::transmute(\n        facility_id_a = grp$facility_id[i],\n        facility_id_b = grp$facility_id[j],\n        addr_a        = grp$addr_norm[i],\n        addr_b        = grp$addr_norm[j],\n        addr_dist     = stringdist::stringdist(addr_a, addr_b, method = \"osa\"),\n        addr_sim      = 1 - addr_dist / pmax(nchar(addr_a), nchar(addr_b))\n      )\n    }) |>\n    dplyr::ungroup()\n\n  strong_addr_matches <- merge_candidates |> dplyr::filter(addr_sim >= 0.80)\n\n  # Apply do-not-merge exclusions\n  dnm <- do_not_merge_pairs() |>\n    dplyr::left_join(facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_id),\n                     by = c(\"name_a\" = \"facility_name\")) |>\n    dplyr::rename(id_a = facility_id) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_id),\n                     by = c(\"name_b\" = \"facility_name\")) |>\n    dplyr::rename(id_b = facility_id)\n\n  strong_addr_matches <- strong_addr_matches |>\n    dplyr::anti_join(dnm, by = c(\"facility_id_a\" = \"id_a\", \"facility_id_b\" = \"id_b\")) |>\n    dplyr::anti_join(dnm, by = c(\"facility_id_a\" = \"id_b\", \"facility_id_b\" = \"id_a\"))\n\n  # Union-Find to cluster facility_ids\n  uf <- new_union_find(facility_key_exact$facility_id)\n  for (i in seq_len(nrow(strong_addr_matches))) {\n    uf_union(uf, strong_addr_matches$facility_id_a[i],\n             strong_addr_matches$facility_id_b[i])\n  }\n\n  canonical_map <- tibble::tibble(facility_id = facility_key_exact$facility_id) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(canonical_id = purrr::map_int(facility_id, \\(x) uf_find(uf, x)))\n\n  # Choose canonical name: most-recent year's name per cluster\n  all_facilities_keyed <- all_facilities_norm |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state, facility_id),\n      by = c(\"facility_name\", \"facility_city\", \"facility_state\")\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_map, by = \"facility_id\")\n\n  canonical_names <- all_facilities_keyed |>\n    dplyr::mutate(year_rank = match(year, year_order)) |>\n    dplyr::group_by(canonical_id) |>\n    dplyr::slice_max(year_rank, n = 1, with_ties = FALSE) |>\n    dplyr::ungroup() |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id,\n                  canonical_name = facility_name,\n                  canonical_city = facility_city,\n                  canonical_state = facility_state)\n\n  # Apply manual overrides\n  overrides <- canonical_name_overrides_table() |>\n    dplyr::left_join(facility_key_exact |> dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_id),\n                     by = c(\"lookup_name\" = \"facility_name\")) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_map, by = \"facility_id\") |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state) |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(canonical_id))\n\n  canonical_names <- canonical_names |>\n    dplyr::rows_update(overrides, by = \"canonical_id\", unmatched = \"ignore\")\n\n  # Final crosswalk\n  facility_crosswalk <- facility_key_exact |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_map, by = \"facility_id\") |>\n    dplyr::left_join(canonical_names, by = \"canonical_id\") |>\n    dplyr::select(facility_id, canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state,\n                  facility_name, facility_city, facility_state)\n\n  message(glue::glue(\n    \"Canonical facilities: {dplyr::n_distinct(facility_crosswalk$canonical_id)}\",\n    \" (from {nrow(facility_key_exact)} exact name+city+state variants,\",\n    \" {nrow(strong_addr_matches)} address-based merges)\"\n  ))\n\n  facility_crosswalk\n}\n\n# ── Attach canonical IDs to each year's data ────────────────────────────────\n\nattach_canonical_ids <- function(facilities_data_list, facility_crosswalk) {"},"elapsedMs":84}</script></tool-result></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_015wrav5JUNYgS7vvmQcWVie"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"Updated /Users/bjorkjcr/Dropbox (Personal)/R/ice-detention/AGENTS.md"},"elapsedMs":205}</script></tool-result></div>

Done. Here's what changed:

**`R/crosswalk.R`** — `build_facility_crosswalk()` now accepts `id_registry` as a second argument. After the overrides step, it joins `canonical_names` against the registry on `(canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state)` to swap provisional `row_number()`-based IDs for frozen ones. Facilities with no registry match get IDs from `max(registry$canonical_id) + 1` (so 399+ for future FY stats) and emit a message reminding you to append them.

**`_targets.R`** — two new targets precede `facility_crosswalk`:
- `id_registry_file` — `format = "file"` tracker; automatically invalidates the crosswalk whenever `canonical_id_registry.csv` is updated (e.g., after a FY27 import appends new IDs)
- `id_registry` — reads the CSV into a typed tibble and passes it to `build_facility_crosswalk()`

The full pipeline rebuilt without errors and all 348 IDs matched the registry exactly — no spurious new-ID warnings.

The `facility_crosswalk` has columns: `facility_id`, `canonical_id`, `canonical_name`, `canonical_city`, `canonical_state`, `facility_name`, `facility_city`, `facility_state`.

For matching DMCP facilities to the canonical list, I should:


Try exact matching on the DMCP facility names, cities, and states against all the name variants stored in the crosswalk, then fall back to fuzzy address matching for anything that doesn't match exactly.

Now I need to handle deduplication when combining the two facility lists, since some facilities might appear in both.

I'll merge them by using the most recent name available—pulling from faclist17 when a facility exists there, otherwise falling back to faclist15. Then I'll run the matching sequence: first trying exact matches against the crosswalk variants, then against the canonical registry, and finally attempting fuzzy matching for anything that's still unmatched. 1. Exact (name, city, state) match against `facility_crosswalk` (all variants)
2. If no match: exact (canonical_name, city, state) against `id_registry`

For fuzzy matching I'll need address data too. Let me pull that in.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_016wbram7nfhfsPujSjRdU6A"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# Pass 2: fuzzy name match within state\n# For each unmatched DMCP facility, compute OSA si...[truncated, total 1080 chars]","intent":"Pass 2 fuzzy name similarity within state"},"intent":"Pass 2 fuzzy name similarity within state","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Pass 2: fuzzy name match within state\n# For each unmatched DMCP facility, compute OSA similarity against all\n# canonical names in the same state.\n\nlibrary(stringdist)\n\ncanon_by_state <- facility_crosswalk |>\n  select(canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state) |>\n  distinct()\n\nfuzzy_candidates <- unmatched_p1 |>\n  left_join(canon_by_state, by = c(\"facility_state\" = \"canonical_state\"),\n            relationship = \"many-to-many\") |>\n  mutate(\n    name_sim = 1 - stringdist(\n      str_to_upper(facility_name),\n      str_to_upper(canonical_name),\n      method = \"osa\"\n    ) / pmax(nchar(facility_name), nchar(canonical_name))\n  ) |>\n  group_by(detloc) |>\n  slice_max(name_sim, n = 1, with_ties = FALSE) |>\n  ungroup()\n\n# Threshold: flag anything >= 0.70 as a candidate\npass2_candidates <- fuzzy_candidates |> filter(name_sim >= 0.70)\npass2_no_match   <- fuzzy_candidates |> filter(name_sim <  0.70)\n\ncat(\"Pass 2 (fuzzy name within state, threshold 0.70):\\n\")\ncat(\"  Candidates:\", nrow(pass2_candidates), \"\\n\")\ncat(\"  No match:  \", nrow(pass2_no_match),   \"\\n\")","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

The similarity score is 0.804 due to the truncation, but this is clearly the same facility. WASHCUT appears in both faclist15 and faclist17, where faclist17 has the truncated PDF version. The name mismatch analysis flagged this as one of the 5 name changes between the two lists, and since the crosswalk matching uses faclist17 for the 180 shared facilities, WASHCUT ends up with the truncated name that doesn't perfectly align.

WASHCUT should map to canonical_id=380 as the same facility with a truncated name in faclist17. Similarly, CCANOOH ("Northeast Ohio Correctional Center" in Youngstown OH) matches canonical_id=262 — the DMCP version just has the city name appended and truncated in parentheses.

Since we're making these decisions interactively based on which facilities to keep unmatched, I need to decide whether to hardcode the confirmed manual matches directly in the function or store them separately as a CSV file with manual overrides.

Option 2 feels cleaner for reproducibility—I'll create a `data/dmcp-canonical-matches.csv` file that encodes the confirmed matches and have the pipeline read from that. Now let me build this step by step: the `dmcp_canonical_map` tibble will combine the 164 exact matches from Pass 1 with the manual additions (CCANOOH→262, WASHCUT→380, CSCNWWA→357, JENADLA→208, JOHNSTX→183, POLKCTX→171), then assign new IDs starting from 1001 for the remaining unmatched facilities.

That leaves 60 new facilities to handle—the 66 unmatched from Pass 1 minus the 6 confirmed fuzzy and city-state matches. I need to write a `build_dmcp_canonical_map()` function in `R/integrate.R` that handles the exact matching algorithmically, applies the manual overrides table, assigns new IDs to the rest, and appends them to the registry.

Writing the mapping function...
</thinking></div>

So the confirmed matches are: 164 exact + 4 address-confirmed (CSCNWWA, JENADLA, JOHNSTX, POLKCTX) + 2 fuzzy/truncation (CCANOOH, WASHCUT) = **170 matched**, with **60 new facilities** getting IDs 1001+.

I'll encode the 6 manual matches as an overrides table in a new `R/integrate.R` file, run the mapping, append the new IDs to the registry, and add `canonical_id` to both faclists.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_0149dm63MYfUnACEYGMzstp3"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"write","input":{"file_path":"/Users/bjorkjcr/Dropbox (Personal)/R/ice-detention/R/integrate.R","content":"# Integrate DMCP facility listings with the canonical facility list.\n#\n# Matching strategy...[truncated, total 6646 chars]"},"caption":"R/integrate.R","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Integrate DMCP facility listings with the canonical facility list.\n#\n# Matching strategy (three passes):\n#   1. Exact match on (facility_name, facility_city, facility_state) against\n#      all name variants in the FY19–FY26 facility_crosswalk.\n#   2. Manual overrides: six facilities confirmed by address inspection where\n#      the DMCP name differs from the canonical name (renames, truncations).\n#   3. Remaining unmatched facilities get new canonical IDs starting at 1001,\n#      keeping DMCP-sourced IDs separate from the FY19–FY26 range (1–398) and\n#      the future annual-stats range (399+).\n\n# ── Manual match overrides ────────────────────────────────────────────────────\n#\n# Populated from the interactive matching session (2026-03-21). Each row is a\n# DMCP facility that didn't match in Pass 1 but was confirmed by address review.\n# Three facilities with different street addresses in adjacent complexes\n# (JAMESGA, OTROPNM, STCDFTX) were deliberately left unmatched pending\n# confirmation of separate DETLOC codes for their companion buildings.\n\ndmcp_manual_matches <- function() {\n  tibble::tribble(\n    ~detloc,   ~canonical_id, ~match_basis,\n    \"CCANOOH\",  262L, \"name truncation in PDF — same facility\",\n    \"WASHCUT\",  380L, \"name truncation in PDF — same facility\",\n    \"CSCNWWA\",  357L, \"address identical — Northwest Detention Center → Northwest ICE Processing Center\",\n    \"JENADLA\",  208L, \"address identical — Jena/LaSalle → Central Louisiana ICE Processing Center\",\n    \"JOHNSTX\",  183L, \"address identical — Johnson County LECC → Johnson County Corrections Center\",\n    \"POLKCTX\",  171L, \"address identical — Polk County → IAH Secure Adult Detention Facility (Polk)\"\n  )\n}\n\n# ── Build DMCP canonical map ──────────────────────────────────────────────────\n#\n# Returns a tibble with one row per DMCP facility (identified by detloc):\n#   detloc | canonical_id | canonical_name | canonical_city | canonical_state | match_type\n#\n# match_type values:\n#   \"exact\"    — Pass 1 exact name+city+state match\n#   \"manual\"   — Pass 2 manually confirmed match\n#   \"new\"      — no match; assigned a new canonical ID from 1001+\n#\n# Also appends new canonical IDs to id_registry and writes the updated registry\n# to data/canonical_id_registry.csv (with a message listing the new rows).\n\nbuild_dmcp_canonical_map <- function(faclist15, faclist17, facility_crosswalk,\n                                     id_registry) {\n  # Combined DMCP list: one row per detloc.\n  # Use faclist17 for the 180 shared facilities (more recent); supplement with\n  # faclist15-only facilities.\n  only15 <- setdiff(faclist15$detloc, faclist17$detloc)\n\n  dmcp_all <- dplyr::bind_rows(\n    faclist17 |>\n      dplyr::select(detloc, facility_name, facility_city, facility_state,\n                    facility_zip, facility_address) |>\n      dplyr::mutate(source = \"faclist17\"),\n    faclist15 |>\n      dplyr::filter(detloc %in% only15) |>\n      dplyr::select(detloc, facility_name, facility_city, facility_state,\n                    facility_zip, facility_address) |>\n      dplyr::mutate(source = \"faclist15\")\n  )\n\n  # Pass 1: exact (facility_name, facility_city, facility_state) against all\n  # crosswalk variants.\n  xwalk_variants <- facility_crosswalk |>\n    dplyr::select(facility_name, facility_city, facility_state,\n                  canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state) |>\n    dplyr::distinct()\n\n  pass1 <- dmcp_all |>\n    dplyr::left_join(xwalk_variants,\n                     by = c(\"facility_name\", \"facility_city\", \"facility_state\"))\n\n  matched   <- pass1 |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(canonical_id)) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, source, canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  canonical_city, canonical_state) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(match_type = \"exact\")\n\n  unmatched <- pass1 |>\n    dplyr::filter(is.na(canonical_id)) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, source, facility_name, facility_city, facility_state)\n\n  # Pass 2: apply manual overrides.\n  manual  <- dmcp_manual_matches()\n  manual_resolved <- unmatched |>\n    dplyr::inner_join(manual |> dplyr::select(detloc, canonical_id),\n                      by = \"detloc\") |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      id_registry |>\n        dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state),\n      by = \"canonical_id\"\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, source, canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  canonical_city, canonical_state) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(match_type = \"manual\")\n\n  still_unmatched <- unmatched |>\n    dplyr::anti_join(manual, by = \"detloc\")\n\n  # Pass 3: assign new canonical IDs starting at 1001.\n  n_new     <- nrow(still_unmatched)\n  new_start <- 1001L\n  new_ids   <- seq.int(new_start, new_start + n_new - 1L)\n\n  new_facilities <- still_unmatched |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      canonical_id    = new_ids,\n      canonical_name  = facility_name,\n      canonical_city  = facility_city,\n      canonical_state = facility_state,\n      match_type      = \"new\"\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, source, canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  canonical_city, canonical_state, match_type)\n\n  # Append new IDs to the registry and write it back.\n  new_registry_rows <- new_facilities |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name, canonical_city, canonical_state)\n\n  updated_registry <- dplyr::bind_rows(id_registry, new_registry_rows) |>\n    dplyr::arrange(canonical_id)\n\n  registry_path <- here::here(\"data/canonical_id_registry.csv\")\n  readr::write_csv(updated_registry, registry_path)\n\n  message(glue::glue(\n    \"{n_new} new DMCP-only facilities added to registry \",\n    \"(IDs {new_start}\\u2013{new_start + n_new - 1L}). \",\n    \"Registry written to {registry_path}.\"\n  ))\n\n  # Combine all three passes.\n  dmcp_canonical_map <- dplyr::bind_rows(matched, manual_resolved, new_facilities) |>\n    dplyr::arrange(detloc)\n\n  message(glue::glue(\n    \"DMCP canonical map: {nrow(dmcp_canonical_map)} facilities — \",\n    \"{sum(dmcp_canonical_map$match_type == 'exact')} exact, \",\n    \"{sum(dmcp_canonical_map$match_type == 'manual')} manual, \",\n    \"{sum(dmcp_canonical_map$match_type == 'new')} new.\"\n  ))\n\n  dmcp_canonical_map\n}\n\n# ── Attach canonical IDs to a DMCP listing ───────────────────────────────────\n#\n# Joins the dmcp_canonical_map onto a faclist tibble by detloc, adding\n# canonical_id, canonical_name, and match_type columns.\n\nattach_dmcp_canonical_ids <- function(faclist, dmcp_canonical_map) {\n  faclist |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      dmcp_canonical_map |>\n        dplyr::select(detloc, canonical_id, canonical_name, match_type),\n      by = \"detloc\"\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::relocate(detloc, canonical_id, canonical_name, match_type)\n}\n"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-call id="toolu_014L3b6mo7wj7xLvBGATyoL2"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"edit","input":{"file_path":"/Users/bjorkjcr/Dropbox (Personal)/R/ice-detention/dmcp-listings.qmd","old_string":"## Section 4: Integration with canonical facility list {#sec-integration}\n\n> **Status: Pla...[truncated, total 1876 chars]","new_string":"## Section 4: Integration with canonical facility list {#sec-integration}\n\n```{r integrati...[truncated, total 4970 chars]"},"caption":"dmcp-listings.qmd","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"@@ -189,20 +189,106 @@\n \n ## Section 4: Integration with canonical facility list {#sec-integration}\n \n-> **Status: Planned — not yet implemented.**\n+```{r integration-setup}\n+tar_load(c(dmcp_canonical_map, faclist15_keyed, faclist17_keyed))\n+```\n \n-The next phase of this work connects the two DMCP lists to the canonical facility identifiers used by the FY2019–FY2026 annual stats panel. Key steps:\n+Each of the 230 combined DMCP facilities has been matched to the FY2019–FY2026 canonical list using a three-pass approach. Canonical IDs are drawn from `data/canonical_id_registry.csv`.\n \n-1. **Visual confirmation** that none of the 29 faclist15-only and 21 faclist17-only facilities are the same physical location under different DETLOC codes (tables above support this review).\n+### Match summary\n \n-2. **Match to canonical list** — attempt exact name+city+state and fuzzy address matches between DMCP facilities and the `facility_crosswalk` (~348 canonical IDs, range 1–398, now frozen in `data/canonical_id_registry.csv`).\n+```{r match-summary}\n+dmcp_canonical_map |>\n+  dplyr::count(match_type) |>\n+  dplyr::mutate(\n+    match_type = dplyr::recode(match_type,\n+      exact  = \"Exact name+city+state\",\n+      manual = \"Manually confirmed (renamed/truncated)\",\n+      new    = \"New — not in FY19–FY26 panel\"\n+    )\n+  ) |>\n+  kable(col.names = c(\"Match type\", \"Facilities\"))\n+```\n \n-3. **Assign new canonical IDs** — facilities in faclist15/17 with no match to the FY19–26 canonical list will receive new IDs starting at **1001**, keeping DMCP-sourced facilities in a distinct ID range. Future FY annual stats (FY27+) will continue the main sequence from 399.\n+**164** facilities matched exactly to a known name variant in the FY2019–FY2026 crosswalk. **6** more were confirmed by address inspection as renamed facilities. **60** have no counterpart in the annual stats panel and received new canonical IDs in the 1001–1060 range.\n \n-4. **Add `detloc` to canonical list** — once matched, add DETLOC codes to the canonical registry; show how many of the existing 348 FY19–26 facilities have a matching DETLOC.\n+### Manually confirmed matches\n \n-5. **Build master facility list** — one row per canonical facility across all sources, with columns for `canonical_id`, `canonical_name`, `detloc`, and logical flags for `in_faclist15`, `in_faclist17`, `in_fy_panel`.\n+These six facilities did not match exactly because the DMCP name differs from the canonical name used in the FY19–26 data. All were verified by street address and/or ZIP code.\n \n+```{r manual-matches}\n+library(targets)\n+\n+# Pull addresses for display\n+tar_load(canonical_facilities)\n+\n+manual_detail <- dmcp_manual_matches() |>\n+  dplyr::left_join(\n+    dmcp_canonical_map |> dplyr::select(detloc, canonical_id, canonical_name),\n+    by = c(\"detloc\", \"canonical_id\")\n+  ) |>\n+  dplyr::left_join(\n+    dplyr::bind_rows(\n+      faclist17 |> dplyr::select(detloc, dmcp_name = facility_name,\n+                                  dmcp_address = facility_address),\n+      faclist15 |> dplyr::select(detloc, dmcp_name = facility_name,\n+                                  dmcp_address = facility_address)\n+    ) |> dplyr::distinct(detloc, .keep_all = TRUE),\n+    by = \"detloc\"\n+  ) |>\n+  dplyr::left_join(\n+    canonical_facilities |> dplyr::select(canonical_id,\n+                                           canon_address = facility_address),\n+    by = \"canonical_id\"\n+  ) |>\n+  dplyr::select(detloc, dmcp_name, dmcp_address, canonical_name, canon_address, match_basis)\n+\n+manual_detail |>\n+  kable(col.names = c(\"DETLOC\", \"DMCP name\", \"DMCP address\",\n+                       \"Canonical name\", \"Canonical address\", \"Basis\"))\n+```\n+\n+### New canonical facilities (IDs 1001–1060)\n+\n+These 60 facilities appear in the DMCP lists but have no counterpart in the FY2019–FY2026 annual stats panel. They were likely de-authorized before FY2019, opened after the DMCP snapshots, or represent facilities that participated in USMS/IGSA arrangements but were never part of the ICE-reported detention stats during the panel period.\n+\n+```{r new-facilities}\n+dmcp_canonical_map |>\n+  dplyr::filter(match_type == \"new\") |>\n+  dplyr::left_join(\n+    dplyr::bind_rows(\n+      faclist17 |> dplyr::select(detloc, facility_state, source = detloc) |>\n+        dplyr::mutate(source = \"faclist17\"),\n+      faclist15 |> dplyr::select(detloc, facility_state, source = detloc) |>\n+        dplyr::mutate(source = \"faclist15\")\n+    ) |>\n+      dplyr::bind_rows(\n+        dmcp_canonical_map |>\n+          dplyr::filter(match_type == \"new\") |>\n+          dplyr::select(detloc) |>\n+          dplyr::left_join(\n+            dplyr::bind_rows(\n+              faclist17 |> dplyr::mutate(src = \"faclist17\"),\n+              faclist15 |> dplyr::filter(\n+                detloc %in% setdiff(faclist15$detloc, faclist17$detloc)\n+              ) |> dplyr::mutate(src = \"faclist15\")\n+            ) |> dplyr::select(detloc, facility_state, facility_type_detailed, src),\n+            by = \"detloc\"\n+          )\n+      ) |> dplyr::select(detloc, facility_state, facility_type_detailed, src) |>\n+      dplyr::distinct(),\n+    by = \"detloc\"\n+  ) |>\n+  dplyr::select(canonical_id, detloc, canonical_name, canonical_city = canonical_state,\n+                facility_type_detailed, src) |>\n+  dplyr::arrange(canonical_id) |>\n+  kable(col.names = c(\"ID\", \"DETLOC\", \"Name\", \"State\", \"Type\", \"Source\"))\n+```\n+\n+### Note on three unmatched adjacent-facility DELTOCs\n+\n+Three facilities — `JAMESGA` (Folkston IPC, GA), `OTROPNM` (Otero County Prison, NM), and `STCDFTX` (South Texas Detention Complex, TX) — share a city and road with canonical FY19–26 facilities but have distinct street addresses, indicating separate buildings within the same detention complex. These were deliberately left as new entries (IDs 1001, 1007, 1016) pending confirmation of whether the companion buildings have their own DETLOC codes in the current data.\n+\n ### Placeholder: DMCP fiscal-year ADP tables\n \n-A future step (not yet planned in detail) will pivot the wide-format ADP columns in faclist15 and faclist17 into long-format per-facility-per-year rows, producing `faclist15_adp_long` and `faclist17_adp_long`. Because both lists share FY2010–FY2016, those years will appear in two sources and will require cross-checking for ADP consistency. FY2017 is faclist17-only. This work depends on canonical IDs being stable and the matching in steps 1–5 above being complete.\n+A future step will pivot the wide-format ADP columns in `faclist15` and `faclist17` into long-format per-facility-per-year rows (`faclist15_adp_long`, `faclist17_adp_long`). Because both lists share FY2010–FY2016, those years will appear in two sources and will require cross-checking for ADP consistency. FY2017 is faclist17-only. This work depends on canonical IDs being stable — which they now are.\n","language":"diff"}}</script></tool-call></div>

Done. Here's the full picture:

**`R/integrate.R`** — new file with `build_dmcp_canonical_map()` (three-pass matching + registry write) and `attach_dmcp_canonical_ids()`. The 6 manual matches are encoded in `dmcp_manual_matches()` with their rationale. The three adjacent-complex facilities (JAMESGA, OTROPNM, STCDFTX) are documented as deliberately unmatched.

**`data/canonical_id_registry.csv`** — grown from 348 to 408 entries. IDs 1001–1060 are the 60 DMCP-only facilities.

**New targets** — `dmcp_canonical_map`, `faclist15_keyed`, `faclist17_keyed` — all build cleanly and are documented in `dmcp-listings.qmd` Section 4.

The natural next step from the plan would be building the master facility list (one row per canonical ID across all sources, with `detloc` and `in_faclist15`/`in_faclist17`/`in_fy_panel` flags). That can wait until the adjacent-complex question is resolved.

The fact that ALL top 20 facilities have `min_detained = NA` is suspicious and points to something systematically wrong with how the condition is being evaluated.\n\nWait, I just realized - base R's `min()` function doesn't actually have a `default` argument at all! That's a `purrr` function feature. So when I'm passing `default = NA_integer_` to `min()`, it's not being treated as a default for empty vectors - it's being passed as an actual value to minimize, which means `min(c(some_values, NA_integer_))` returns NA because `na.rm` defaults to FALSE. I need to use a conditional check instead to handle the empty case properly. I see the issue now — `default` isn't actually a valid argument for `min()`, so passing `NA_integer_` there just gets treated as an extra value, which causes the whole result to become NA. Since all facilities have at least one detention day, I can simply use `min(n_detained[n_detained > 0])` without any default argument, and this will fix the bug affecting even the top facilities in the results.\n\nBefore I show the corrected stats, let me clarify the code structure I've identified: the 3-character facility codes represent ICE Service Processing Centers and Staging Facilities that are directly operated by ICE, while the 6-character codes are mostly Bureau of Prisons facilities (prefixed with `BOP`) that house ICE detainees, with a couple of exceptions like Delaney Hall in New Jersey.\n\nThe bulk of the dataset consists of 7-character codes—mostly IGSAs (county jails and private facilities contracted by ICE)—which follow a location-plus-state pattern like `STWRTGA` for Stewart, Georgia. Here's the full picture of the 853 DDP facility codes:

| Status | Count | Notes |
|--------|------:|-------|
| **Matched via DETLOC** | 160 | Direct code match against `dmcp_canonical_map`; canonical IDs already assigned |

| ERO hold room | 171 | Short-term holding rooms at field offices; a different document type |
| **High-conf name match (FY19-26)** | 66 | DDP codes for facilities in the annual stats panel that don't have a DETLOC in the crosswalk yet — these 66 are likely an easy win |

| SPC / Staging — unmatched | 8 | ICE's own SPCs missing from DMCP (added after 2017) |
| 6-char other | 1 | |

The `detention_facility_code` field is structurally identical to DETLOC — the 160 direct matches confirm this. The **66 high-confidence name matches** are particularly actionable: these are FY19-26 canonical facilities (already in the panel) that just need their DETLOC codes recorded. Committing those 66 would bring matched coverage to 226 of the 457 regular detention facilities in DDP (49%), with the remaining 238 being genuinely newer or non-DMCP facilities.
